25:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part. Be mindful of God, and He will teach you: He has full knowledge of everything26:T1626,<entryFree id="n36563" key="كَبُرَ" type="main">

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36582-1" target="كِبْرٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n36569"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36582-2" target="كِبْرَةٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n36575"/></foreign> [in like manner] signify <hi rend="ital">a great sin,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">crime,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">offence, for which one deserves punishment:</hi> (M, K:) the <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> is to give intensiveness to the signification: (TA:) or   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36582-3" target="كِبْرٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n36569"/></foreign> signifies [simply] <hi rend="ital">a sin, a crime,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an offence, for which one deserves punishment,</hi> [as <foreign lang="ar">كَبِيرَةٌ</foreign> is said, not well, to signify, in the Msb,] and is from <foreign lang="ar">كَبِيرَةٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">خِطْ</foreign> from <foreign lang="ar">خَطِيْئَةٌ</foreign>: (TA:) pl. of the first, <foreign lang="ar">كَبَائِرُ</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">كَبِيرَاتٌ</foreign> also occurs. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And see <foreign lang="ar">كَبِيرٌ</foreign>.    </entryFree>2f:T1881,<entryFree id="n36586" key="أَكْبَرُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَكْبَرُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [<hi rend="ital">Greater,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">greatest, in body,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">corporeal substance,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">in estimation</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rank</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dignity:</hi> and] <hi rend="ital">more,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">most, advanced in age; older,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">oldest:</hi> (Msb:) fem. <foreign lang="ar">كُبْرَى</foreign>: (S, Msb:) pl. masc. <foreign lang="ar">أَكَابِرُ</foreign> (S, Msb) and <foreign lang="ar">أَكْبَرُونَ</foreign>; but not <foreign lang="ar">كُبْرٌ</foreign>, because this is of a form specially appropriated to an epithet such as <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَحْمَرُ</foreign>, and you do not use <foreign lang="ar">اكبر</foreign> in the manner of such an epithet, for you do not say <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا رَجُلٌ أَكْبَرُ</foreign>, unless you conjoin it with a following word by <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign>, or prefix to it the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>: (S:) [but see the phrase <foreign lang="ar">دَعَا بِكُبْرِهِ</foreign>, below:] the pl. fem. is <foreign lang="ar">كُبَرٌ</foreign> (S, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">كُبْرَيَاتٌ</foreign>. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَكْبَرُ</foreign> is also used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">كَبِيرٌ</foreign>: (Msb:) accord. to some, <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُ أَكْبَر</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">God is great;</hi> (Az, Mgh, Msb;) like as <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ أَهْوَنُ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> [in the Kur, xxx. 26,] means <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ هَيِّنٌ عَلَيْهِ</foreign>; (Az, TA;) but this explanation is of weak authority: (Mgh:) accord. to others, the phrase is elliptical, and means <hi rend="ital">God is the greatest great</hi> [<hi rend="ital">being</hi>]: (Az, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">God is greater than every</hi> [<hi rend="ital">other</hi>] <hi rend="ital">great</hi> [<hi rend="ital">being</hi>]: (Msb:) or <hi rend="ital">greater than every</hi> [<hi rend="ital">other</hi>] <hi rend="ital">thing:</hi> (Mgh, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">greater than such as that one knows the measure of His majesty:</hi> (TA:) [or it may be rendered <hi rend="ital">God is most great,</hi> meaning, greater than any other being:] it is considered as elliptical because it is necessary that <foreign lang="ar">اكبر</foreign> should have the article <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign>, or be followed by a noun in the gen. case [or by the prep. <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign>]. (TA.) In the phrase <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُ أَكْبَرُ كَبِيراً</foreign>, the word <foreign lang="ar">كبيرا</foreign> is put in the accus. case [as a corroborative] in the place of the inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَكْبِيراً</foreign>, as though one said <foreign lang="ar">أُكَبِّرُ تَكْبِيرًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I magnify</hi> Him <hi rend="ital">greatly,</hi> after saying <foreign lang="ar">اللّٰه اكبر</foreign>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمُ الحَجِّ الأَكْبَرِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The day of the greater pilgrimage,</hi>] means <hi rend="ital">the day of the sacrifice:</hi> or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">the day of 'Arafeh:</hi> and others say otherwise. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  In the following words, in a trad. of Mázin, <foreign lang="ar">بُعِثَ نَبِىٌّ مِنْ مُضَرَ بِدِينِ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الكُبَرِ</foreign>, there is an ellipsis, and the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">بِشَرَئِعِ دِينِ ٱللّٰهِ الكُبَرِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A prophet of Mudar hath been sent with the greatest,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">greater,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">great, ordinances of God</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  In a trad. respecting burial, <foreign lang="ar">وَيُجْعَلُ ٱلْأَكْبَرُ مِمَّا يَلِى ٱلْقِبْلَةَ</foreign> means, <hi rend="ital">And the most excellent shall be placed towards the Kibleh:</hi> or, if they be equal [in dignity], <hi rend="ital">the oldest.</hi> (TA.) [Agreeably with the former rendering,] <foreign lang="ar">أَكْبَرُ</foreign>, in the Kur, xxix. 44, is explained as signifying <hi rend="ital">Better.</hi> (TA, art. <foreign lang="ar">ذكر</foreign>.) [And agreeably with the second rendering of the above trad.,] you say <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا أَكْبَرُ مِنْ زَيْدٍ</foreign>, meaning, <hi rend="ital">This is older than Zeyd.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  In a trad. of Ibn-Ez-Zubeyr, the phrase <foreign lang="ar">دَعَا بِكُبْرِهِ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">He summoned his sheykhs,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">elders,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">great men:</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كُبْر</foreign> being here [notwithstanding what has been said above,] pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أَكْبَرُ</foreign>, like as <foreign lang="ar">حُمْرٌ</foreign> is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أَحْمَرُ</foreign>. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">هٰذِهِ الجَارِيَةُ مِنْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كُبْرَى بَنَاتِ فُلَانٍ</foreign> means, [<hi rend="ital">This girl is of those advanced in age of the daughters of such a one,</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ كِبَارِ بَنَاتِهِ</foreign>. (Ibn-Buzurj.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ أَكْبَرُ قَوْمِهِ</foreign>: see <foreign lang="ar">كِبْرَةٌ</foreign>.    </entryFree>30:T46c,<entryFree id="n36592" key="المُتَكَبِّرُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">المُتَكَبِّرُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, as an epithet applied to God, signifies <hi rend="ital">The Great in majesty:</hi> (A:) or <hi rend="ital">the Most Excellent of beings, who has rights which no other has; the Possessor of power and excellence the like of which no other possesses:</hi> (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">He whose acts are really good, exceeding the good acts of any other:</hi> (El-Basáïr:) or, as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36592-1" target="الكَبِيرُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, <hi rend="ital">the Majestic:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">He who disdains having the attributes of created beings:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">He who magnifies Himself against the proud and exorbitant among his creatures:</hi> the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> in the former word is to denote individuation, not endeavour.
